## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics ŌĆö nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, naturally modeled by Newtonian equations of motion for oscillators where acceleration depends on restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possible external/parametric forcing (functions of t). With features (x, v, t), this aligns with nonlinear harmonic oscillator families such as Duffing and van der Pol systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper with linear friction)
- Time-varying stiffness (parametric oscillator): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric excitation / Mathieu-type structure)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos in forced regime)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag-dominated damping at higher speeds)
- Nonlinear velocity damping (cubic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Coulomb (dry) friction oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (stick-slip type idealization with constant-magnitude friction)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle via state-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excited oscillation via velocity-dependent damping)
- Nonlinear restoring from saturating stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 + c2 * x / (1 + c3 * x**2) - c4 * v (effective spring that softens/hardens then saturates)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically depend on x only and are odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - c*x**3), reflecting symmetry about x=0.
- Damping forces typically oppose motion: terms like -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), or -c*sign(v) reduce energy and stabilize the equilibrium.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior is often captured by state-dependent damping terms such as (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v, which inject energy at small amplitude and dissipate at large amplitude.
- Periodic external driving appears as additive sin/cos of t (e.g., +c*cos(c*t)), producing resonance peaks and possibly chaos when combined with nonlinearity (Duffing).
- Parametric excitation appears by making the stiffness multiply x with periodic t dependence, e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, enabling parametric resonance bands.
- Hardening vs softening springs correspond to the sign of the cubic stiffness term in -c1*x**3, leading to amplitude-dependent frequency shifts.
- Non-smooth dissipation (sign(v), Abs(v)) indicates dry friction or impacts and can create piecewise dynamics (sticking/rapid transitions).
- Cross terms coupling x and v (e.g., x**2*v) often indicate nonlinear damping or coupling through geometry/material effects, changing decay rates with amplitude.

\[

Even ignoring extra removable terms (by setting coefficients to 0), **none** of the candidates include:
- a \(v\sin(x)\) term (sine is only in \(t\) in all candidates), and
- an \(x\exp(-|x|)\) term (no candidate has \(\exp(-|x|)\) or any \(|x|\) dependence).

Therefore no parameter choice can make any candidate identical to the GT for all real \(x,t,v\).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO43)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.748007302808642*v*(1 - x**2) - 0.377828837635262*v*sin(x) - 0.755657675270524*v - 3.87049024210282*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.26471389821047*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
`0.748007302808642*v*x**2 - 0.748007302808642*v - 0.377828837635262*v*sin(x) - 0.755657675270524*v - 3.87049024210282*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.26471389821047*sin(t)`

Combining v terms:
`0.748007302808642*v*x**2 - 1.503665978079166*v - 0.377828837635262*v*sin(x) - 3.87049024210282*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.26471389821047*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v*x**2` ŌĆö linear in v, quadratic in x
2. `v` ŌĆö linear
3. `v*sin(x)` ŌĆö product of v and sin(x)
4. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` ŌĆö product of x and exp(-|x|)
5. `sin(t)` ŌĆö sinusoidal in t

Key observations:
- The term `v*sin(x)` is unique ŌĆö it requires a product of v with sin(x)
- The term `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is unique ŌĆö it requires x times an exponential of |x|
- These are specific basis functions that cannot be replicated by polynomials, power laws, logarithms, or simple products

Now let me check each candidate:

**Every candidate** uses combinations of terms like: `v`, `sin(t)`, `x**c`, `v*x**2`, `v*x`, `v**4`, `log(...)`, `exp(c*t)`, `x**3`, `v**3*x`, `(c+t)**(-4)`, constants, etc.

**Critical missing basis functions in ALL candidates:**
1. **`v*sin(x)`**: None of the candidates contain a term that is a product of `v` and `sin(x)`. This is a linearly independent basis function that cannot be generated from any combination of the terms present in the candidates.
2. **`x*exp(-Abs(x))`**: None of the candidates contain `x*exp(-|x|)`. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be exactly represented by power laws `x**c`, polynomials, logarithms, or any other basis functions present in the candidates.

Since `v*sin(x)` and `x*exp(-|x|)` are linearly independent from all basis functions appearing in every candidate, and their coefficients in the GT are non-zero (-0.3778... and -3.8705...), **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify there's no hidden way to generate these: `x*exp(-|x|)` is not a power law ŌĆö `x**c` for any fixed c cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. Similarly, `v*sin(x)` cannot be produced from `v*x`, `v*x**2`, `v*x**3`, or any polynomial/power combination.
